–î–æ—Å—Ç–æ–≤–µ—Ä–Ω—ã—Ö –¥–∞–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –æ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è—Ö –æ–±–µ–∏—Ö —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω –≤ —ç—Ç–æ–π —Å—Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∫–µ —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å –Ω–µ—Ç, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –∞–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Ç–∏–∫ CIT –ö–∏—Ä–∏–ª–ª –ú–∏—Ö–∞–π–ª–æ–≤, –Ω–æ —Å—É–¥—è –ø–æ¬†[–ø—É–±–ª–∏–∫–∞—Ü–∏–∏](https://www.economist.com/europe/2022/09/04/ukraine-is-losing-fewer-soldiers-in-its-counter-offensive-than-russia-claims)
¬†The Economist (–∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Å—Ç—ã –ø–æ–±—ã–≤–∞–ª–∏ –≤ –ø—Ä–∏—Ñ—Ä–æ–Ω—Ç–æ–≤–æ–º –≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥–µ –ù–∏–∫–æ–ª–∞–µ–≤–µ, –ø–æ–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª–∏ —Å –º–µ—Å—Ç–Ω—ã–º–∏ –≤—Ä–∞—á–∞–º–∏ –∏ –Ω–µ —É–≤–∏–¥–µ–ª–∏ —Ç–∞–º ¬´–ø–µ—Ä–µ–ø–æ–ª–Ω–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –º–æ—Ä–≥–æ–≤¬ª —Å –ø–æ–≥–∏–±—à–∏–º–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–º–∏ –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–º–∏, –æ —á–µ–º —É—Ç–≤–µ—Ä–∂–¥–∞–µ—Ç —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∞—è —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω–∞), —Ö–æ—Ç—å –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –≤—ã—Ä–æ—Å–ª–∏ —Å –Ω–∞—á–∞–ª–æ–º –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è, –æ–Ω–∏ –Ω–µ –∫–∞—Ç–∞—Å—Ç—Ä–æ—Ñ–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–µ, –∫–∞–∫ —ç—Ç–æ –∑–∞—è–≤–ª—è–µ—Ç —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–µ –ú–∏–Ω–æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã. –ü–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º –±—ã–≤—à–µ–≥–æ —Å–æ—Ç—Ä—É–¥–Ω–∏–∫–∞ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π —Å–ø–µ—Ü—Å–ª—É–∂–±—ã, —Å –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–º –ø–æ–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª–∏ ¬´–í–∞–∂–Ω—ã–µ –∏—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–∏–∏¬ª, –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã –≤—ã—Å–æ–∫–∏, –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—é—â–∞—è —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω–∞ –≤—Å–µ–≥–¥–∞ —Ç–µ—Ä—è–µ—Ç –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—è—é—â–µ–π—Å—è.

–ù–∞ —Ç—Ä–µ—Ç–∏–π –¥–µ–Ω—å –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ The Wall Street Journal¬†[–ø–æ–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª–∞](https://www.wsj.com/articles/ukrainian-soldiers-say-they-are-advancing-in-the-south-but-at-a-cost-11661983338)
¬†–≤ –≥–æ—Å–ø–∏—Ç–∞–ª–µ —Å —Ä–∞–Ω–µ–Ω—ã–º–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–º–∏ —Å–æ–ª–¥–∞—Ç–∞–º–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ —É—á–∞—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞–ª–∏ –≤ –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏. –ü–æ –∏—Ö —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º, –±–æ–∏ –Ω–∞ –ø—É—Ç–∏ –∫ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—É –∏–¥—É—Ç –∫—Ä–∞–π–Ω–µ –æ–∂–µ—Å—Ç–æ—á–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ, –Ω–æ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–µ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–≤–∏–≥–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –≤–ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥. ¬´–£ –Ω–∏—Ö –º–Ω–æ–≥–æ —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∏, –Ω–æ –º–∞–ª–æ –ª—é–¥–µ–π¬ª, ‚Äî —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª –æ–¥–∏–Ω –∏–∑ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö. –ö—Ä–æ–º–µ —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ, –æ–Ω–∏ —É—Ç–≤–µ—Ä–∂–¥–∞—é—Ç, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–µ–∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–µ —Å–æ–ª–¥–∞—Ç—ã –±–µ–≥—É—Ç —Å–æ —Å–≤–æ–∏—Ö –ø–æ–∑–∏—Ü–∏–π, –±—Ä–æ—Å–∞—è —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫—É –∏ —É—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–∞–≤–ª–∏–≤–∞—è –º–∏–Ω—ã –Ω–∞ —Ç–µ–ª–∞—Ö –ø–æ–≥–∏–±—à–∏—Ö —Ç–æ–≤–∞—Ä–∏—â–µ–π.

–ü–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º –æ–¥–Ω–æ–≥–æ –∏–∑ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏—Ö, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–π —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∞—è –∞—Ä–º–∏—è —Ç–∞–º –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è –≤ —Ç—è–∂–µ–ª–æ–º –ø–æ–ª–æ–∂–µ–Ω–∏–∏, —Å–æ–ª–¥–∞—Ç—ã –º–∞—Å—Å–æ–≤–æ –ø—ã—Ç–∞—é—Ç—Å—è —É–≤–æ–ª–∏—Ç—å—Å—è. ¬´–î–≤–µ –Ω–µ–¥–µ–ª–∏ –Ω–∞–∑–∞–¥ –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥–∏—Ä—ã –Ω–∞–º —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–∏, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–∞ –Ω–∞—Å –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ –∏–¥–µ—Ç. –ê –Ω–∞–º –¥–∞–∂–µ –±–æ–µ–ø—Ä–∏–ø–∞—Å—ã –Ω–∏–∫–∞–∫ –Ω–µ –ø—Ä–∏–≤–µ–∑—Ç–∏, –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ –¥–∞–º–±–∞ —Ä–∞–∑–±–∏—Ç–∞ (_–≤–µ—Ä–æ—è—Ç–Ω–æ, —Ä–µ—á—å –∏–¥–µ—Ç –æ –¥–∞–º–±–µ –≤ –ù–æ–≤–æ–π –ö–∞—Ö–æ–≤–∫–µ_¬†‚Äî¬†**–ü—Ä–∏–º. —Ä–µ–¥.**). –õ—é–¥–∏ –∫–∞–∂–¥—ã–π –¥–µ–Ω—å —Ö–æ–¥—è—Ç —Å —Ä–∞–ø–æ—Ä—Ç–∞–º–∏ \[–Ω–∞ —É–≤–æ–ª—å–Ω–µ–Ω–∏–µ\], –Ω–æ –ø–æ—á—Ç–∏ –≤—Å–µ–º –∏—Ö —Ä–∞–∑—Ä—ã–≤–∞—é—Ç¬ª, ‚Äî –Ω–∞–ø–∏—Å–∞–ª –æ–Ω. –°–ø—É—Å—Ç—è –¥–≤–µ –Ω–µ–¥–µ–ª–∏ –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π –ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥–∞–ª ¬´–í–∞–∂–Ω—ã–º –∏—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–∏—è–º¬ª, —á—Ç–æ –ø—Ä–∏ –æ–±—Å—Ç—Ä–µ–ª–µ —á—É–¥–æ–º –≤—ã–∂–∏–ª, –∏ ¬´—Ç–∞–º –≤—Å–µ –∂–µ—Å—Ç–∫–æ¬ª.

–î—Ä—É–≥–æ–π –∏—Å—Ç–æ—á–Ω–∏–∫, –±–ª–∏–∑–∫–∏–π –∫ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–º –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏–º, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥—è—Ç—Å—è –Ω–∞ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏, –ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥–∞–ª, —á—Ç–æ —Å–æ–ª–¥–∞—Ç—ã –≤ –ø–æ–ª–Ω–æ–º —à–æ–∫–µ, ¬´–Ω–∏–∫—Ç–æ –Ω–∏—á–µ–≥–æ –Ω–µ –ø–æ–Ω–∏–º–∞–µ—Ç, –≥–∏–±–Ω—É—Ç –ø–∞—á–∫–∞–º–∏, –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–∏ —É–∂–∞—Å–Ω—ã–µ. –ù–µ–∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –≤–æ–æ–±—â–µ –∑–≤–æ–Ω—è—Ç, –ø—Ä–æ—â–∞—é—Ç—Å—è, –º—ã, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä—è—Ç, —Å–º–µ—Ä—Ç–Ω–∏–∫–∏ –µ–±—É—á–∏–µ¬ª.

### **–£ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º—ã —Å–æ —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ–º**

–ï—â–µ –æ–¥–Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º–∞ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω–∞ —Å–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∏–≤–∞—Ç—å –ø—Ä–æ—Ä—ã–≤ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –∑–∞–∫–ª—é—á–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è –≤ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ –æ–Ω–∞ –æ–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–∞—Å—å –æ—Ç—Ä–µ–∑–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–π –æ—Ç –≤—Å–µ—Ö –æ—Å–Ω–æ–≤–Ω—ã—Ö –ø—É—Ç–µ–π —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏—è. –†–∞–Ω–µ–µ —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫–∏ –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–º –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥—É –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–∏—Å—Ö–æ–¥–∏–ª–æ —á–µ—Ä–µ–∑ –º–æ—Å—Ç—ã, –ø–æ –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–º –≤–µ–∑–ª–∏ –±–æ–µ–ø—Ä–∏–ø–∞—Å—ã, —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫—É, —Ç–æ–ø–ª–∏–≤–æ –∏ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–æ–≤–æ–ª—å—Å—Ç–≤–∏–µ —Å –ª–µ–≤–æ–≥–æ –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥–∞ —Ä–µ–∫–∏. –û–¥–Ω–∞–∫–æ –≤ —Ä–µ–∑—É–ª—å—Ç–∞—Ç–µ —É–¥–∞—Ä–æ–≤ –í–°–£ –≤—Å–µ —Å—Ç–∞—Ü–∏–æ–Ω–∞—Ä–Ω—ã–µ –º–æ—Å—Ç—ã —á–µ—Ä–µ–∑ –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä –±—ã–ª–∏ –≤—ã–≤–µ–¥–µ–Ω—ã –∏–∑ —Å—Ç—Ä–æ—è, –ø–æ–Ω—Ç–æ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –∏ –ø–∞—Ä–æ–º–Ω—ã–µ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–ø—Ä–∞–≤—ã –ø–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–Ω–æ –ø–æ–¥–≤–µ—Ä–≥–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –æ–±—Å—Ç—Ä–µ–ª–∞–º.

¬´\[–ò—Å—Ö–æ–¥ —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–∏–≤–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–∏—è –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–º –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥—É –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–∞\] –∑–∞–≤–∏—Å–∏—Ç –æ—Ç —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —É–¥–∞—Å—Ç—Å—è –ª–∏ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏—è–Ω–∞–º –æ—Ä–≥–∞–Ω–∏–∑–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –ø–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∫–∏ \[—Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏—è\] –ø–∞—Ä–æ–º–∞–º–∏, –ø–æ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫—É –≤—Å–µ –ø–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –º–æ—Å—Ç—ã –ø–µ—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–∞–ª–∏ —Ñ—É–Ω–∫—Ü–∏–æ–Ω–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å. –ù–∞–ª–∞–¥–∏—Ç—å –ø–æ–Ω—Ç–æ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–ø—Ä–∞–≤—ã —á–µ—Ä–µ–∑ –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä \[—Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏\] –Ω–µ —É–¥–∞–ª–æ—Å—å. –°–µ–π—á–∞—Å —Ñ—É–Ω–∫—Ü–∏–æ–Ω–∏—Ä—É–µ—Ç –Ω–µ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –ø–∞—Ä–æ–º–Ω—ã—Ö –ø–µ—Ä–µ–ø—Ä–∞–≤ ‚Äî –∏—Ö —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Ü–∞–º —Ç—è–∂–µ–ª–µ–µ –ø–æ—Ä–∞–∂–∞—Ç—å, —á–µ–º –º–æ—Å—Ç—ã, –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ –ø–∞—Ä–æ–º—ã –º–æ–±–∏–ª—å–Ω—ã, —Å–ª–æ–∂–Ω–æ –ø—Ä–µ–¥—É–≥–∞–¥–∞—Ç—å, –≥–¥–µ –æ–Ω–∏ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥—è—Ç—Å—è.

–û–¥–Ω–∞–∫–æ –ø–µ—Ä–∏–æ–¥–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Ü—ã –ø—ã—Ç–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –ø–æ—Ä–∞–∂–∞—Ç—å —Å–∫–æ–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∏ –≤ –º–µ—Å—Ç–∞—Ö –æ–∂–∏–¥–∞–Ω–∏—è –ø–∞—Ä–æ–º–æ–≤. –≠—Ç–æ –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω–æ –≤—ã–∑—ã–≤–∞—Ç—å –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º—ã —Å–æ —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ–º. –ù–∞—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏—è–Ω–∞–º —Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∏—Ç —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å–æ–≤ –¥–ª—è –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–∏–≤–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–∏—è, –∑–∞–≤–∏—Å–∏—Ç –æ—Ç —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —Å–º–æ–≥—É—Ç –ª–∏ –æ–Ω–∏ —ç—Ñ—Ñ–µ–∫—Ç–∏–≤–Ω–æ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–±—Ä–∞—Å—ã–≤–∞—Ç—å –ø–æ–¥–∫—Ä–µ–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ, –∞ —Ç–∞–∫–∂–µ –æ—Ç —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞—Ç—Å—è —Å–∏–ª—ã –í–î–í, –ø–æ–∫–∞ —É –Ω–∏—Ö –Ω–µ –∑–∞–∫–æ–Ω—á–∏—Ç—Å—è —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∞, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è –Ω–µ –æ—Ç–ª–∏—á–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è –±—Ä–æ–Ω–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å—é¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –∞–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Ç–∏–∫ CIT –ö–∏—Ä–∏–ª–ª –ú–∏—Ö–∞–π–ª–æ–≤.

### **–ß–µ–º –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–∏ –≥—Ä–æ–∑–∏—Ç –ø—Ä–æ–¥–≤–∏–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ –í–°–£**¬†

–û—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∏–µ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–º–∏ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞–º–∏ –Ω–∞—Å–µ–ª–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–≥–æ –ø—É–Ω–∫—Ç–∞ –í—ã—Å–æ–∫–æ–ø–æ–ª—å–µ –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ 4 —Å–µ–Ω—Ç—è–±—Ä—è —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞–ª–æ –Ω–µ–≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω—ã–º –¥–ª—è —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –≤–µ–¥–µ–Ω–∏–µ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã—Ö –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏–π –≤ –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –ö—Ä–∏–≤–æ–≥–æ –†–æ–≥–∞ –≤ –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–æ–ø–µ—Ç—Ä–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ. ¬´–≠—Ç–æ –±—ã–ª–∞ –∫—Ä–∞–π–Ω—è—è —Å–µ–≤–µ—Ä–Ω–∞—è —Ç–æ—á–∫–∞, –æ—Ç–∫—É–¥–∞ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏—è–Ω–µ –º–æ–≥–ª–∏ —Ä–∞–∑–≤–µ—Ä–Ω—É—Ç—å –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—É—é –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏—é –≤ –ö—Ä–∏–≤–æ—Ä–æ–∂—Å–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏. –í –Ω–∞—Å—Ç–æ—è—â–µ–µ –≤—Ä–µ–º—è —ç—Ç–∏ –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ —É –Ω–∏—Ö –æ—Ç—Å—É—Ç—Å—Ç–≤—É—é—Ç, ‚Äî –æ–±—ä—è—Å–Ω—è–µ—Ç –æ–Ω.

‚Äî –ö—Ä–æ–º–µ —Ç–æ–≥–æ, –±–ª–∞–≥–æ–¥–∞—Ä—è –í—ã—Å–æ–∫–æ–ø–æ–ª—å—é –í–°–£ –ø–æ–ª—É—á–∏–ª–∏ –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å —Ä–∞—Å—à–∏—Ä–∏—Ç—å –ø–ª–∞—Ü–¥–∞—Ä–º –≤ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–±–µ—Ä–µ–∂–Ω–æ–π —á–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –∏ —Å—Ñ–æ—Ä–º–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å —É—Å–ª–æ–≤–∏—è –¥–ª—è –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è –Ω–∞ –¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç–æ—á–Ω–æ —É–≥—Ä–æ–∂–∞—é—â–µ–º —É—á–∞—Å—Ç–∫–µ –¥–ª—è –º–Ω–æ–≥–∏—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –í–° –†–§. –ï—Å–ª–∏ –í–°–£ –±—É–¥—É—Ç –¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç–æ—á–Ω–æ —É—Å–ø–µ—à–Ω–æ —Ä–∞–∑–≤–∏–≤–∞—Ç—å –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏—è, —Ç–æ –º—ã —Å–º–æ–∂–µ–º –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç—å –æ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ –æ–≥—Ä–æ–º–Ω–æ–µ –∫–æ–ª–∏—á–µ—Å—Ç–≤–æ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –æ–∫–∞–∑–∞—Ç—å—Å—è —Ñ–∞–∫—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ –≤ –æ–∫—Ä—É–∂–µ–Ω–∏–∏¬ª.

–°—Ç—Ä–∞—Ç–µ–≥–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–π –∏ –ø–æ–ª–∏—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–π —Å–º—ã—Å–ª –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏ –Ω–∞ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –¥–ª—è –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—ã –≤ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã —Ä–∞–∑–≥—Ä–æ–º–∏—Ç—å —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫—É—é –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫—É –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–º –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥—É –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–∞ –∏ –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–¥–∏—Ç—å –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω, —Å—á–∏—Ç–∞–µ—Ç –∞–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Ç–∏–∫ CIT –ö–∏—Ä–∏–ª–ª –ú–∏—Ö–∞–π–ª–æ–≤. ¬´–≠—Ç–æ –ø–æ–∑–≤–æ–ª–∏—Ç –∑–∞–¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å —ç–∫–æ–Ω–æ–º–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–µ —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å—ã –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –∞ —Ç–∞–∫–∂–µ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–µ–º–æ–Ω—Å—Ç—Ä–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –∑–∞–ø–∞–¥–Ω—ã–º –ø–∞—Ä—Ç–Ω–µ—Ä–∞–º –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—ã \[–ø–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤—â–∏–∫–∞–º –æ—Ä—É–∂–∏—è\], —á—Ç–æ —Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω–∞ –≤ —Å–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–∏–∏ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç—å –∏ –≤—ã–∏–≥—Ä—ã–≤–∞—Ç—å ‚Äî –Ω—É–∂–Ω–æ —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ \[–ø–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–æ–∫\] –æ—Ä—É–∂–∏—è.

–ö—Ä–æ–º–µ —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ, –≤ –¥–æ–ª–≥–æ—Å—Ä–æ—á–Ω–æ–π –ø–µ—Ä—Å–ø–µ–∫—Ç–∏–≤–µ –ª–∏–∫–≤–∏–¥–∞—Ü–∏—è –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–±–µ—Ä–µ–∂–Ω–æ–≥–æ –ø–ª–∞—Ü–¥–∞—Ä–º–∞ —É—Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω—è–µ—Ç –ø–µ—Ä—Å–ø–µ–∫—Ç–∏–≤—É –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è \[—Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏\] –Ω–∞ –ù–∏–∫–æ–ª–∞–µ–≤, –ö—Ä–∏–≤–æ–π –†–æ–≥ –∏ –û–¥–µ—Å—Å—É, –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ –∏–º–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –∑–∞—Ö–≤–∞—Ç –º–æ—Å—Ç–æ–≤ –∏ –≤—ã—Ö–æ–¥ –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤—ã–π –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥ –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–∞ –±—ã–ª —Å–∞–º—ã–º –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–º —É—Å–ø–µ—Ö–æ–º —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏—è–Ω –Ω–∞ –ø–µ—Ä–≤–æ–º —ç—Ç–∞–ø–µ –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏. –õ–∏–∫–≤–∏–¥–∞—Ü–∏—è —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –ø–ª–∞—Ü–¥–∞—Ä–º–∞ —Å–∏–ª—å–Ω–æ —Å–Ω–∏–∂–∞–µ—Ç —É–≥—Ä–æ–∑—É –≤—Å–µ–π –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–±–µ—Ä–µ–∂–Ω–æ–π –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω–µ, –≤ —Ç–æ–º —á–∏—Å–ª–µ –∑–∞–ø–∞–¥–Ω–æ–º—É –ß–µ—Ä–Ω–æ–º–æ—Ä—å—é, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–µ –∫—Ä–∏—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ –≤–∞–∂–Ω–æ –¥–ª—è –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—ã —Å —Ç–æ—á–∫–∏ –∑—Ä–µ–Ω–∏—è, –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∏–º–µ—Ä, —ç–∫—Å–ø–æ—Ä—Ç–∞ —Å–µ–ª—å—Ö–æ–∑–ø—Ä–æ–¥—É–∫—Ü–∏–∏¬ª, ‚Äî –æ–±—ä—è—Å–Ω—è–µ—Ç —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏–º–æ—Å—Ç—å –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏ –Ω–∞ —ç—Ç–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏.

–ì–¥–µ –µ—â–µ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—é—Ç –í–°–£ –∏ –∫–∞–∫–∞—è –±–∏—Ç–≤–∞ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç —Ä–µ—à–∞—é—â–µ–π
--------------------------------------------------

–ö—Ä–æ–º–µ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –∏ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–µ–π, –í–°–£ –æ—Å—É—â–µ—Å—Ç–≤–ª—è—é—Ç –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏—è –≤ –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ. –í —á–∞—Å—Ç–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω –Ω–∞—Å–µ–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π –ø—É–Ω–∫—Ç –û–∑–µ—Ä–Ω–æ–µ –≤ –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏. ¬´–ê–Ω–∞–ª–æ–≥–∏—á–Ω—ã–µ –Ω–æ–≤–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –±—É–¥—É—Ç –ø–æ—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç—å –∏ –∏–∑ –õ—É–≥–∞–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –≥–¥–µ –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ –∞–∫—Ç–∏–≤–∏–∑–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–ª–∏—Å—å –í–°–£, –≤–æ—Å–ø–æ–ª—å–∑–æ–≤–∞–≤—à–∏—Å—å –æ—Å–ª–∞–±–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ–º —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –ø–æ—Å–ª–µ –¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç–æ—á–Ω–æ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–æ–ª–∂–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–≥–æ –≤–æ–∑–¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏—è –Ω–∞ –Ω–∏—Ö –æ–≥–Ω–µ–≤—ã–º –ø–æ—Ç–µ–Ω—Ü–∏–∞–ª–æ–º¬ª, ‚Äî —É–≤–µ—Ä–µ–Ω —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç.

–ü–æ –º–Ω–µ–Ω–∏—é –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ, —Ä–µ—à–∞—é—â–µ–π –¥–ª—è —ç—Ç–æ–π –≤–æ–π–Ω—ã –±–∏—Ç–≤–æ–π —Å—Ç–∞–Ω–µ—Ç –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –≤ –ó–∞–ø–æ—Ä–æ–∂—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏. ¬´–ë–∏—Ç–≤–∞ –∑–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–±–µ—Ä–µ–∂–Ω—É—é –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—â–∏–Ω—É ‚Äî —ç—Ç–æ –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –≤–∞–∂–Ω—ã–π –ø—Ä–æ–º–µ–∂—É—Ç–æ—á–Ω—ã–π —ç—Ç–∞–ø. –ü–æ—Å–ª–µ –µ–µ –∑–∞–≤–µ—Ä—à–µ–Ω–∏—è –∏ –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∏—è –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω–∞ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∞ –∏ –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–∞—è —á–∞—Å—Ç—å —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å–æ–≤ –í–°–£, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –±—ã–ª–∏ –∑–∞–¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞–Ω—ã –¥–ª—è —Å–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∏–≤–∞–Ω–∏—è —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –æ–∫–∫—É–ø–∞–Ω—Ç–æ–≤ –∏ –¥–ª—è –≤–µ–¥–µ–Ω–∏—è —ç—Ç–æ–π –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–π –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏. –ò —ç—Ç–∏ —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å—ã –º–æ–≥—É—Ç –±—ã—Ç—å –∏—Å–ø–æ–ª—å–∑–æ–≤–∞–Ω—ã –Ω–∞ –¥—Ä—É–≥–∏—Ö –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è—Ö: –ó–∞–ø–æ—Ä–æ–∂—Å–∫–æ–π, –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π, –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü–∫–æ–π –∏ –õ—É–≥–∞–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—è—Ö.

–û–Ω–∏ —Å—ã–≥—Ä–∞—é—Ç —Ä–µ—à–∞—é—â—É—é —Ä–æ–ª—å –≤ –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–º —É—Å–∫–æ—Ä–µ–Ω–∏–∏, —É–≤–µ–ª–∏—á–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –∞–∫—Ç–∏–≤–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –∏ –∏–Ω—Ç–µ–Ω—Å–∏–≤–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏–π –í–°–£. –î–ª—è –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∏—è —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≤–æ–π—Å–∫ –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –≤–∞–∂–Ω–æ —Å–æ—Ö—Ä–∞–Ω—è—Ç—å –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–æ–ª—å –∏–º–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –Ω–∞–¥ –ó–∞–ø–æ—Ä–æ–∂—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å—é. –ï–µ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è –¥–ª—è —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏—è–Ω ‚Äî —ç—Ç–æ —Ñ–∞–∫—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ –≤—ã—Å—Ç—Ä–µ–ª –≤ –≤–∏—Å–æ–∫, –ø–æ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫—É —ç—Ç–æ —Å—Ç–∞–Ω–µ—Ç –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–µ–π –≤—Å–µ–≥–æ —é–≥–∞, –∞ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è –≤—Å–µ–≥–æ —é–≥–∞ ‚Äî —ç—Ç–æ –∏ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è –ö—Ä—ã–º–∞. –í—ã–π–¥—è –≤ –ó–∞–ø–æ—Ä–æ–∂—Å–∫—É—é –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å, –í–°–£ –ø–æ–ª—É—á–∞—Ç –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å –±–ª–æ–∫–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –ö—Ä—ã–º —Å –º–∞—Ç–µ—Ä–∏–∫–æ–≤–æ–π —á–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—ã –∏ –Ω–∞–Ω–µ—Å—Ç–∏ —É–¥–∞—Ä—ã –ø–æ –ö–µ—Ä—á–µ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–º—É –º–æ—Å—Ç—É ‚Äî —Ç–æ –µ—Å—Ç—å –æ—Ç—Ä–µ–∑–∞—Ç—å –µ–≥–æ –æ—Ç –º–∞—Ç–µ—Ä–∏–∫–æ–≤–æ–π —á–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–∏ –∏ –Ω–∞—á–∞—Ç—å –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏—é –ø–æ –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∏—é –ö—Ä—ã–º–∞¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –æ–Ω.

## Elaboration
The evidence indicates that Russia protested the participation of US private military companies (PMCs) fighting alongside Ukraine in the Kursk region, with the incursion beginning on the night of August 5-6, 2024. Newsweek reported on August 20, 2024, that Russia claimed to have seen evidence of American mercenaries participating in the incursion, and the U.S. denied involvement. The claim aligns with these reports.

The image in the claim shows individuals with what appears to be US flags on their uniforms. This visual evidence supports the claim that American mercenaries were involved. However, the evidence does not confirm the image's authenticity or the exact date and location of the photo.

To fully verify the claim, additional information is needed to confirm the image's origin and the identity of the individuals depicted.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "<image:24> This image shows American mercenaries participating in Ukraine's incursion into Russia's Kursk Oblast in August 2024."

## Evidence
### Evidence from `web_search`
Newsweek reports that Russia claims to have seen evidence of American mercenaries participating in Ukraine's incursion into Russia's Kursk Oblast, and the U.S. has denied involvement. The article was published on August 20, 2024. ([https://www.newsweek.com/russia-protests-american-soldiers-kursk-1942273](https://www.newsweek.com/russia-protests-american-soldiers-kursk-1942273))

The Anadolu Agency published an article on August 20, 2024, stating that Russia protested the participation of US private military companies (PMCs) fighting alongside Ukraine in the Kursk region. The incursion into the Kursk region began on the night of August 5-6. ([https://www.aa.com.tr/en/russia-ukraine-war/russia-formally-protests-us-mercenaries-joining-ukrainian-soldiers-in-kursk-region-/3308755](https://www.aa.com.tr/en/russia-ukraine-war/russia-formally-protests-us-mercenaries-joining-ukrainian-soldiers-in-kursk-region-/3308755))

## Elaboration
The evidence indicates that Russia protested the participation of US private military companies (PMCs) fighting alongside Ukraine in the Kursk region, with the incursion beginning on the night of August 5-6, 2024. Newsweek reported on August 20, 2024, that Russia claimed to have seen evidence of American mercenaries participating in the incursion, and the U.S. denied involvement. The claim aligns with these reports.

The image in the claim shows individuals with what appears to be US flags on their uniforms. This visual evidence supports the claim that American mercenaries were involved. However, the evidence does not confirm the image's authenticity or the exact date and location of the photo.

To fully verify the claim, additional information is needed to confirm the image's origin and the identity of the individuals depicted.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `web_search`
   * Description: Run an open web search on Google or DuckDuckGO to retrieve any related webpage.
   * How to use: Do not use this with a previously used or similar query from previous web searches. If a previous web search did not yield any results, use a very different query.
   * Format: web_search("your web search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

Armed Forces Day (Poland)

From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

National holiday in Poland

| Armed Forces Day |     |
| --- | --- |
| [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Polish_M1_Abrams.jpg/330px-Polish_M1_Abrams.jpg)](/wiki/File:Polish_M1_Abrams.jpg)<br><br>Armed Forces Day 2023, Warsaw |     |
| Official name | ≈öwiƒôto Wojska Polskiego |
| Observed¬†by | Poland |
| Significance | [Battle of Warsaw (1920)](/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)") |
| Celebrations | [Military parades](/wiki/Military_parade "Military parade")<br>, equipment reviews, silences |
| Begins | 13:00 [CET](/wiki/Central_European_Time "Central European Time") |
| Date | 15 August |
| Next¬†time | 15 August 2025¬†(2025-08-15) |
| Frequency | annual |

**Armed Forces Day**, known also as the **Feast of the Polish Armed Forces** ([Polish](/wiki/Polish_language "Polish language")
: _≈öwiƒôto Wojska Polskiego_), is a national holiday celebrated annually on 15 August in Poland, commemorating the anniversary of the 1920 victory over [Soviet Russia](/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic "Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic")
 at the [Battle of Warsaw](/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)")
 during the [Polish‚ÄìSoviet War](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish‚ÄìSoviet War")
.[\[1\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2013-1)
 Armed Forces Day is held in conjunction with the [Day of the Assumption of the Virgin Mary](/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary "Assumption of Mary")
, itself a separate public holiday.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)
 The event is marked by [military parades](/wiki/Military_parade "Military parade")
, equipment reviews, showcases and remembrances by all branches of the [Polish Armed Forces](/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces "Polish Armed Forces")
 across the country. To commemorate the republic's victory over the Red Army, Minister of Military Affairs [Stanis≈Çaw Szeptycki](/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Szeptycki "Stanis≈Çaw Szeptycki")
 established the Feast of the Soldier (_≈öwiƒôta ≈ªo≈Çnierza_), or Soldiers Day, in 1923.[\[4\]](#cite_note-4)
 In proclaiming the holiday, Szeptycki declared that, "\[o\]n the anniversary of the memorable defeat of the Bolshevik onslaught on Warsaw, we honor the memory of those killed in battles with enemies throughout all ages and for Polish independence."[\[5\]](#cite_note-Museum-5)
 The date of 15 August was chosen as it coincided with the [21st Mountain Division's](/wiki/21st_Mountain_Infantry_Division_(Poland) "21st Mountain Infantry Division (Poland)")
 evening counterattack on Russian troops, eventually forcing the Red Army's general retreat.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)
 Additionally, the government of the Second Republic desired the military's greater integration with the new state, as well as for the armed forces to improve its image among the civilian public.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)

The Feast of the Soldier remained a celebrated holiday until 1947, when the newly installed communist government of the [People's Republic of Poland](/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Poland "People's Republic of Poland")
 discontinued the tradition.[\[6\]](#cite_note-Gazeta2013-6)
 In 1950, the [Council of Ministers](/wiki/Cabinet_of_Poland "Cabinet of Poland")
 under Prime Minister [J√≥zef Cyrankiewicz](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Cyrankiewicz "J√≥zef Cyrankiewicz")
 passed regulations to officially celebrate the military on 12 October.[\[7\]](#cite_note-DzU1950-7)
 Renaming the celebration as Polish Armed Forces Day (_Dzie≈Ñ Wojska Polskiego_), the day marked the anniversary of the Soviet-organized [Polish 1st Tadeusz Ko≈õciuszko Infantry Division](/wiki/Polish_1st_Tadeusz_Ko%C5%9Bciuszko_Infantry_Division "Polish 1st Tadeusz Ko≈õciuszko Infantry Division")
 engaging [German](/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany")
 units at the [Battle of Lenino](/wiki/Battle_of_Lenino "Battle of Lenino")
 in October 1943.[\[7\]](#cite_note-DzU1950-7)
 The communist government found it impossible to celebrate the original date of 15 August and its coinciding historical significance, owing to its glorification of the [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army")
's defeat.[\[8\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2012-8)
 Following the return of democracy in the wake of the [events of 1989](/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989 "Revolutions of 1989")
, the [Sejm](/wiki/Sejm "Sejm")
 approved the restoration of Armed Forces Day to the original 15 August date and meaning on 30 July 1992, repealing the earlier communist era 1950 declaration.[\[9\]](#cite_note-Sejm1992-9)

Commemorations
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Armed_Forces_Day_(Poland)&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: Commemorations")\
\]

Armed Forces Day is celebrated throughout Poland, with military parades, commemorations for active personnel, veterans, and the dead. As head of state and [commander-in-chief](/wiki/Commander-in-chief "Commander-in-chief")
, the [President of Poland](/wiki/President_of_Poland "President of Poland")
 presides over promotions of high-ranking officers, including the promotion of colonels to generals at the [Presidential Palace](/wiki/Presidential_Palace,_Warsaw "Presidential Palace, Warsaw")
.[\[1\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2013-1)
 The pageantry continues with commemorations near the [Tomb of the Unknown Soldier](/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Unknown_Soldier,_Warsaw "Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, Warsaw")
 held in [Pi≈Çsudski Square](/wiki/Pi%C5%82sudski_Square "Pi≈Çsudski Square")
.[\[11\]](#cite_note-Prezydent-11)
 The events in Warsaw typically involve the participation of the nation's political establishment, including the [president](/wiki/President_of_Poland "President of Poland")
, the [prime minister](/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Poland "Prime Minister of Poland")
, and leading members of the [cabinet](/wiki/Cabinet_of_Poland "Cabinet of Poland")
.[\[6\]](#cite_note-Gazeta2013-6)
 Leading politicians also lay wreaths at the [J√≥zef Pi≈Çsudski](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski "J√≥zef Pi≈Çsudski")
 Monument, as well as at the [Tomb of the Unknown Soldier](/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Unknown_Soldier,_Warsaw "Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, Warsaw")
.[\[6\]](#cite_note-Gazeta2013-6)

As a [NATO](/wiki/NATO "NATO")
 member state, Armed Forces Day in Poland typically draws representatives from other allied militaries in attendance.[\[12\]](#cite_note-12)

The centennial celebrations for 2020 were "1920 Battle of Warsaw ‚Äì a Polish victory for the freedom of Europe".[\[13\]](#cite_note-13)

### Armed Forces Day Parade

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Armed_Forces_Day_(Poland)&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Armed Forces Day Parade")\
\]

One of the main attractions of the Warsaw festivities is a [military parade](/wiki/Military_parade "Military parade")
 of servicemen and women, as well as a review of existing military equipment, held normally along [Ujazd√≥w Avenue](/wiki/Ujazd%C3%B3w_Avenue "Ujazd√≥w Avenue")
.[\[11\]](#cite_note-Prezydent-11)
 Active servicemen and women participate at many events, joined often by volunteers appearing in historical dress, including those donning the equipment and dress of the [Polish‚ÄìSoviet War](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War "Polish‚ÄìSoviet War")
 or other historical periods.[\[1\]](#cite_note-PolskieRadio2013-1)
 The first grand military parades since the holiday was reinstated in Warsaw were in 2007 and 2008, and parades have been held yearly since 2013. In 2019, the parade took place in the southern city of [Katowice](/wiki/Katowice "Katowice")
 to honour the participation of [Silesia](/wiki/Silesia "Silesia")
's residents in the [Silesian Uprisings](/wiki/Silesian_Uprisings "Silesian Uprisings")
 from 1919 to 1921.[\[14\]](#cite_note-14)

14. One of the most prominent events of the day is in the capital Warsaw, which hosts a large military parade through the city's center. Originally celebrated during the [Second Republic](/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic "Second Polish Republic")
, the holiday was barred by authorities during the communist era beginning in 1947, only to be revived again in 1992.[\[3\]](#cite_note-3)

History
-------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Armed_Forces_Day_(Poland)&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: History")\
\]

Main article: [Battle of Warsaw (1920)](/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920) "Battle of Warsaw (1920)")

In the event known by the critics as the "Miracle of the Vistula," the [Polish Army](/wiki/Polish_Army "Polish Army")
 under the command of Marshal [J√≥zef Pi≈Çsudski](/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski "J√≥zef Pi≈Çsudski")
 successfully repulsed a [Red Army](/wiki/Red_Army "Red Army")
 offensive outside of Warsaw in mid-August 1920. As the day coincides with the religious [Day of the Assumption](/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary "Assumption of Mary")
, church masses across the country reflect on the memory of Poland's military dead.[\[2\]](#cite_note-Kontakt24-2)
 Additionally, a number of military-themed events are held throughout many of the nation's larger towns and cities, including equipment demonstrations for the general public and open house events.[\[10\]](#cite_note-TVNWarszawa-10)

In Warsaw, the holiday is commemorated by several state events in the central [≈ör√≥dmie≈õcie](/wiki/%C5%9Ar%C3%B3dmie%C5%9Bcie,_Warsaw "≈ör√≥dmie≈õcie, Warsaw")
 borough of the capital."

A rehearsal ahead of the Armed Forces Day parade in Warsaw, Aug."

# Your Summary



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The Polish Ministry of Defence announced a military parade on August 15, 2024, as part of a four-day celebration from August 14 to 17. The parade will showcase military hardware, including South Korean-made K2 battle tanks, Polish-produced Krab self-propelled gun-howitzers, and US-made M1A1 Abrams tanks. The event is an expression of "strength, agency and unity" in the face of "threats from the East." <image:25> is not mentioned in the article.

From [Source](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armed_Forces_Day_(Poland)): 
Content: The search result is from Wikipedia and discusses Armed Forces Day in Poland, celebrated annually on August 15th. It commemorates the 1920 victory over Soviet Russia at the Battle of Warsaw. The day is marked by military parades, equipment reviews, and commemorations. The article mentions that military parades are held, and in 2019, the parade took place in Katowice. <image:25> is not in the search result.


From [Source](https://www.polskieradio.pl/395/7784/artykul/3413138,poland-set-for-massive-military-parade):

The parade will showcase military hardware, including South Korean-made K2 battle tanks, Polish-produced Krab self-propelled gun-howitzers, and US-made M1A1 Abrams tanks. The event is an expression of "strength, agency and unity" in the face of "threats from the East." <image:25> is not mentioned in the article.


## Your Summary



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The Associated Press reported on Poland's military parade on August 15, 2024, as part of the annual Armed Forces Day observances in Warsaw, showcasing its growing army and modern equipment. (<image:25>) The Polish Ministry of Defence announced a military parade on August 15, 2024, as part of a four-day celebration from August 14 to 17, showcasing military hardware. The event is an expression of "strength, agency and unity" in the face of "threats from the East." (<image:25>)

The Armed Forces Day in Poland is celebrated annually on August 15th, commemorating the 1920 victory over Soviet Russia at the Battle of Warsaw, marked by military parades and equipment reviews. (<image:25>)

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "<image:25> This image shows a military parade of Poland's army on August 14, 2024, preparing for war with Russia."

## Actions
```
reverse_search(<image:25>)
web_search("Poland military parade August 14 2024")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `web_search`
The Associated Press reported on Poland's military parade on August 15, 2024, as part of the annual Armed Forces Day observances in Warsaw, showcasing its growing army and modern equipment. (<image:25>) The Polish Ministry of Defence announced a military parade on August 15, 2024, as part of a four-day celebration from August 14 to 17, showcasing military hardware. The event is an expression of "strength, agency and unity" in the face of "threats from the East." (<image:25>)

The Armed Forces Day in Poland is celebrated annually on August 15th, commemorating the 1920 victory over Soviet Russia at the Battle of Warsaw, marked by military parades and equipment reviews. (<image:25>)

*   [https://apnews.com/article/poland-armed-forces-day-russia-army-parade-db5c8663bf0b6e3c403b0c8482da4aed](https://apnews.com/article/poland-armed-forces-day-russia-army-parade-db5c8663bf0b6e3c403b0c8482da4aed)

# Your Analysis



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The image depicts a military parade in Poland. The parade was part of the Armed Forces Day celebrations on August 15, 2024, and included a four-day celebration from August 14 to 17. The event showcased military hardware and was an expression of strength in the face of threats.

The claim that the parade was preparing for war with Russia is not directly supported by the evidence. While the event was held in the context of "threats from the East," the evidence does not explicitly state that the parade was a preparation for war.

Therefore, the claim is partially accurate, as the parade did occur on August 14, 2024. However, the claim that it was preparing for war with Russia is not directly supported by the evidence.

2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.



## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
